    "synthesis": {
      "executiveSummary": "The OrbGuard product is a polished UI shell over a largely disconnected system. The 274 findings (77 critical, 111 high) cluster into four systemic failure modes rather than isolated bugs: (1) CLIENT-SERVER CONTRACT DIVERGENCE — the Flutter app and Go backend were built against different schemas; on virtually every feature (dashboard summary, SMS analysis, URL check, QR scan, scam indicators, campaigns/actors/sources lists, device security, WiFi audit, app analysis, forensics) the request keys, response keys, paths, or enums do not match, so real backend data is silently discarded and screens render empty or fall back to fabricated local data. (2) FABRICATED DATA PRESENTED AS REAL — the analytics service, SMS/network/app stats, app reputation, TTP similarity, and dashboard threat score return hardcoded literals; the client compounds this with hardcoded fallbacks (fake IOC stats of 2,500, invented footprint scan of 12 brokers, score-100 device status, random-number scan progress), meaning failures are indistinguishable from clean results — unacceptable in a security product. (3) UNWIRED INFRASTRUCTURE — main.go constructs the ScamDetector with an empty config (LLM/pattern-DB/phone/vision/speech all disabled), passes nil for Safe Browsing and all five desktop-security services (entire /desktop surface 503s), never starts ML training despite AutoTrain:true, and the backend keeps dark-web assets, device-security state, removal requests, URL lists, firewall rules, and gateway-MAC baselines in process memory (some globally shared across users — a privacy defect). (4) MISSING CAPABILITY LAYERS — the com.orb.guard/wifi, supply_chain, firewall, tflite, and app_update native channels have zero platform implementations; there is no device agent for the anti-theft loop; forensics asks users to type server-side file paths for phone backups (architecturally impossible); the VPN/DNS-protection tabs have neither endpoints nor on-device mechanisms. Production secrets (HIBP/LeakCheck/IntelX keys) are hardcoded in shipped client source and must be rotated immediately. Net assessment: the backend contains genuinely good analysis engines (WiFi audit, IOC scanner, code-signing verifier, correlation engine) that are unreachable from the product. Roughly a fifth of the system works end-to-end today; the path to production is dominated by wiring and contract alignment, not greenfield work, and is highly parallelizable across the six waves below.",
